id="ctl00_ctl00_MainContent_uxProduct_uxProductTabs_ProductTabs_body" class="ajax__tab_body ajax__scroll_vert"> <div id="ctl00_ctl00_MainContent_uxProduct_uxProductTabs_ProductTabs_pnlFeatures" class="ajax__tab_panel" style="visibility: visible;"> <div class="Features"> <span id="ctl00_ctl00_MainContent_uxProduct_uxProductTabs_ProductTabs_pnlFeatures_ProductFeatureDesc"><h2><font style="color: #000000;">RUGER</font></h2> <h2><font style="color: #000000;"><span>SR1911 .45 ACP 5 Inch Barrel Low Glare Stainless Steel Finish, Includes one 8 Round and one 7 Round Magazine</span></font></h2> <p><span><font face="book antiqua,palatino" size="3"><span>Original 1911 Series 70 design. Hardwood grips and checkered backstrap. CNC machined. Stainless steel barrel and bushing are produced from the same bar stock on the same machine for improved accuracy. Positive barrel lock-up. Oversized ejection port and extended magazine release. Lightweight aluminum skeletonized trigger features an adjustable over-travel stop. Dovetailed 3-dot sight system features a Novak LoMount Carry rear and standard front sight. Includes titanium firing pin, one 7-round and one 8-round stainless steel magazine, bushing wrench.</span></font><br></span></p> <h2><span>Enthusiasts Enjoy. Competition Beware.</span></h2> <p><font size="3">Introducing the <strong>RUGER SR1911,</strong>&nbsp;a classically styled pistol designed with all of the modern manufacturing advances that you have come to expect from Ruger. Accurate, rugged and reliable, the SR1911 is 100% American-made in American factories with American workers. <strong>Enthusiasts enjoy. Competition beware.</strong></font></p> <p><span class="h1">From the Ruger Press Room</span></p> <h2><span class="headline"><img src="../../../../Data/Default/Images/uploads/ruger/2011-04-18.jpg" alt="Ruger SR1911" hspace="5" vspace="5" width="125" height="125" align="left">Ruger Introduces All American-Made SR1911 Pistol</span><span class="date">&nbsp;</span></h2> <p><span class="date">April 18, 2011</span> <br><span class="Copy">&nbsp;</span></p> <p><span class="Copy">Sturm, Ruger &amp; Company, Inc. (NYSE: RGR) is proud to announce the Ruger SR1911, an "All American" classic rendition of John Browning's most famous handgun design. The public debut of the Ruger SR1911 pistol will take place during the NRA Annual Meeting in Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania April 29 - May 1.<br><br>The single-action .45 Auto Ruger SR1911 features a bead-blasted stainless steel frame and slide, precision CNC machined for a precise slide-to-frame fit. The stainless steel barrel and bushing are produced simultaneously, from the same ordnance-grade barstock, for a precise fit and improved accuracy. The slide features rear cocking serrations and a dovetailed three-dot sight system with a Novak rear sight and standard front sight.<br><br>"We are very proud to offer a 1911 pistol, an icon of American gun design and manufacturing," said Ruger CEO Michael Fifer. "In this 100-anniversary year of the introduction of the Government Model 1911 it is only fitting that such a firearm be completely manufactured in America with all American-made components."<br><br>The Ruger SR1911 pistol features a titanium firing pin and heavy firing pin spring, which negates the need for a firing pin block, offering an updated safety feature to the original "Series 70" design without compromising trigger pull weight. An extended thumb safety offers improved manipulation and an oversized beavertail grip safety provides positive function and reliability. A visual inspection port offers visual confirmation of a round in the chamber.<br><br>Positive extraction is facilitated by an improved internal extractor. The plunger tube for both the slide stop and thumb safety is integral to the frame and will never shoot loose. The swedged link pin also will not shoot loose. The SR1911 uses a skeletonized hammer and an aluminum, skeletonized trigger with an adjustable over-travel stop. The Ruger SR1911 features a standard recoil guide system and flat mainspring housing.<br><br>The Ruger SR1911 grips feature a Ruger logo in checkered hardwood panels. Each pistol is shipped with one 7-round and one 8-round stainless steel magazine, bushing wrench and a soft case. The SR1911 will fit currently available holsters.</span></p> <p>&nbsp;</p> <p><span class="Copy"> <object width="425" height="350" data="http://www.youtube.com/v/wAP9bLqM6Ss&amp;feature" type="application/x-shockwave-flash"> <param name="data" value="http://www.youtube.com/v/wAP9bLqM6Ss&amp;feature"> <param name="src" value="http://www.youtube.com/v/wAP9bLqM6Ss&amp;feature"> </object> <br></span></p> <p><span class="h1">Ruger SR1911 Features</span></p> <p><font size="3"><strong>CLASSIC STYLE: </strong>Original 1911 Series 70 design provides for easy takedown and re-assembly. Slim traditional design</font><font size="3"> with hardwood grips and checkered backstrap.</font></p> <p><font size="3"><strong>MODERN MANUFACTURING:</strong> Precision CNC-controlled machining process &nbsp;results in a superior slide-to-frame fit</font><font size="3"> and smooth slide travel. The stainless steel barrel and bushing are produced from the same bar stock, on the same</font><font size="3"> machine, for improved accuracy.</font></p> <p><font size="3"><strong>PERFORMANCE:</strong> Positive barrel lock-up allows for a superior accuracy out-of-the-box. Oversized ejection port and</font><font size="3"> extended magazine release enhance competition performance.</font></p> <p><font size="3"><strong>TRIGGER AND HAMMER:</strong> Lightweight, aluminum, skeletonized trigger features an adjustable over-travel stop and</font><font size="3"> provides a very crisp, no creep, light trigger pull with a quick, positive reset. Skeletonized hammer is lightweight and</font><font size="3"> provides faster cycling.</font></p> <p><font size="3"><strong>SIGHTING SYSTEM:</strong> Dovetailed, 3-dot sight system features a Novak LoMount Carry rear and standard front sight that</font><font size="3"> combines optimal target acquisition in an ideal carry configuration.</font></p> <p><font size="3"><strong>FRAME AND SLIDE:</strong> Stainless steel frame and slide feature blasted, low-glare finish and slide serrations for positive grip.</font></p> <p><font size="3"><strong>SAFETY:</strong> Oversized beavertail grip safety provides positive function and reliability. Extended thumb safety and slide stop lever provide for improved, positive manipulation. Visual inspection port allows for visual confirmation that chamber is loaded.</font></p> <p><font size="3"><img src="../../../../Data/Default/Images/uploads/ruger/ruger_1911_b.jpg" alt="" width="474" height="330"></font></p> <p>&nbsp;</p> <p><font size="3"><img src="../../../../Data/Default/Images/uploads/ruger/ruger_1911_c.jpg" alt="" width="454" height="617"></font></p> <p><font size="3"><img src="../../../../Data/Default/Images/uploads/ruger/ruger_1911_d.jpg" alt="" width="444" height="438"></font></p> <p><font size="3"><img src="../../../../Data/Default/Images/uploads/ruger/ruger_1911_e.jpg" alt="" width="592" height="421"></font></p> <p><font size="3"><img src="../../../../Data/Default/Images/uploads/ruger/ruger_1911_f.jpg" alt="" width="639" height="440"></font></p> <p><font size="3"><img src="../../../../Data/Default/Images/uploads/ruger/ruger_1911_g.jpg" alt="" width="686" height="407"><br></font></p></span></div> </div><div I didn't give them 5 stars because their triggers have a lot of up and down movement and a bit of slack to be taken up before firing. They're also no where near as crisp of a let off as my Kimber. Both slides also have a bit of play between them and the frame, both up and down and side to side. Not much, but they're not a rock solid fit. That could actually be a good thing for reliability. Their accuracy is about the same as my Glock, good but not great. I also found the bottom edge of the main spring housing checkering to be a bit abrasive on my hand. Other then those small details, they have been great guns. I've since used my dremmel to polish the feed ramps, changed the safeties out for the stainless standard colt safety since I hate the extended versions, and changed the main spring housings out for the a stainless chain link type that's much easier on my palms but still grippy. These additions cost me about $50 total and some time to do the fitting. All in all, I'm very happy with the pistols, and for the price I don't feel bad about subjecting them to rough duty use. I know this review was long, but I hope its raw honesty helped.</div> <div class="Row"> By <span class="Text"> Will</span> from <span class="Text"> Florida</span></div> </div> </div> </td> </tr><tr>
